No Rain in Hubei Province for Two Months, Severe Autumn Drought

(Hankou) There has been no rain in Hubei Province for two months, and the autumn drought is serious. Forty-seven counties have been affected, with agricultural losses of 10 million dan. According to the unified assessment of autumn harvests, only 70% will be obtained. The current climate is humid and hot like summer, and epidemic malaria is widespread. The Hubei Farmers' Association and the Agricultural Bank decided on the 24th to borrow 1 million yuan to set up agricultural warehouses to help farmers. (Special Dispatch, 24th)

Yangtze River Water Level Declines Day by Day

(Nanjing) There has been no rain in the Yangtze River area for two months, and the inland rivers in various places have dried up, causing traffic jams. The water level of the rivers is declining day by day, and grain prices are rising, and wheat cannot be planted. A drought cannot be avoided. According to the investigation of the Yangtze River water level on the 24th, Zhenjiang is 2.10 meters, down 0.61 meters; Nanjing is 3.20 meters, down 0.34 meters; Wuhu is 3.17 meters, down 0.40 meters; Datong is 6.60 meters, down 0.50 meters; Anqing is 4.24 meters, down 0.50 meters; Jiujiang is 4.94 meters, down 0.43 meters; Hankou is 4.88 meters, down 0.27 meters. The water level of the Grand Canal is Qingjiang 7.39 meters, down 0.06 meters; Shiying 5.34 meters, down 0.15 meters; Gaoyou 4.67, down 0.15 meters; Shaobo 2.64, down 0.15 meters. (Special Dispatch, 24th)

Huang Musong, Zeng Yangfu, Hu Yisheng, Hu Mulan, and several hundred others greeted them at the station. (Hong Kong) Sun Ke, Chen Lifu, Wang Chonghui, Shao Yuanchong, Jiao Yitang, Li Wenfan, Liang Hancao, and their entourage, along with Guangdong welcome representatives Li Xuhuan, Liu Weichi, Liu Shixin, and over one hundred others, departed from Hong Kong at 9:40 AM on the 24th via a special train on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway to participate in the state funeral ceremony for the late Chairman Hu. Lin Yunhai, Xie Wuliang and others had traveled ahead by ship on the 23rd. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

(Nanjing) As the state funeral for the late Chairman Hu is scheduled for the 25th, all sectors of the capital have decided to hold a public memorial ceremony at 9:00 AM on the 25th in the auditorium of the Nanjing City Party Headquarters, presided over by Zhou Fu, a special commissioner of the Party Headquarters. All entertainment in the city will be suspended, and all government agencies, organizations, schools, shops, and residences will fly flags at half-mast for one day in mourning. The City Party Headquarters has specially issued a letter to comrades and compatriots regarding the state funeral for the late Chairman Hu. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

The embassy community also intends to fly flags at half-mast to show their solidarity. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

Legislative Yuan to Discuss Insurance Law

(Nanjing) The Insurance Law, the Insurance Industry Law, and the Insurance Industry Implementation Law, which were reviewed, revised, and passed by the Commercial Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan, may be submitted again to the Yuan's meeting next week for discussion. The revised Insurance Law includes three chapters: General Provisions, Property Insurance, and Personal Insurance, totaling one hundred articles, which is a significant supplement to the one promulgated in the eighteenth year of the Republic. The revised Insurance Industry Law only changes the "Property Insurance" within it to "Property Loss Insurance," in accordance with the Insurance Law, to ensure uniformity. The Insurance Industry Implementation Law consists of twenty articles, which stipulate that the Ministry of Actual Affairs may establish insurance supervisors in areas where the insurance industry is flourishing to supervise the insurance industry. In other areas, the Construction Department or the Social Affairs Bureau will be in charge. The security deposit that the insurance industry should pay according to law has also been stipulated and should be deposited into the national treasury within six months after the implementation of the Insurance Industry Law. Insurance contracts stipulate that Chinese characters should be used. In view of the extremely developed insurance business in China in recent years, the Commercial Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan has specially revised and formulated the above three cases to facilitate promulgation and implementation and to meet social needs. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

Control Yuan to Investigate Civil Servants Using Drugs

(Nanjing) The Control Yuan previously approved a public letter from the Chairman of the Military Commission and concurrently the Director-General of the Anti-Smoking Bureau regarding the case of reporting Party, government, and military service personnel smoking opium and using drugs. It had previously been submitted to the National Government to be forwarded to subordinate agencies for implementation. However, it has been heard that Party, government, and military service personnel inside and outside the capital still secretly use drugs. At a time when smoking and drugs are strictly prohibited, if Party, government, and military personnel cannot be purged, what explanation can be given to the general public? It is specially requested that the Control Yuan conduct a serious investigation. The Control Yuan approved the consultation and has ordered each supervising inspector to conduct extensive investigations, truthfully report, and strictly investigate and handle the matter. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

Writing and Photos of the Horse Show in Suiyuan (Part 2)

— Zong Liangdong

The competition began at noon. At the sound of the silver horn on the rostrum, tens of thousands of spectators craned their necks and applauded, eager to see who would win. The competition began with a preliminary round of pacing horses, with a distance of one li. Seventy horses participated, in groups of five, with a qualification standard of a non-disrupted pace within one minute and twenty seconds. The next was the preliminary round of running horses, with 140 horses participating in 18 groups, each group also consisting of five horses. The distance was three li, and the qualification standard was a speed within two minutes and fifty seconds. On the first day of the preliminary round, 77 running horses and 28 pacing horses qualified. On the second day, the running horses in the semi-final had to reach the finish line within two minutes and forty-five seconds, while the pacing horses had to do so within one minute and sixteen seconds. Changes in gait were limited to three times or less; more than that would result in disqualification.

The second day of the competition happened to be a Sunday, and the crowd was even more congested than on the first day. The double semi-final for pacing horses started in the morning, and the show of colts and mules began in the afternoon. First, the committee members and referees examined them. The standard for the show was: (1) pure Mongolian breed; (2) healthy and sound reproductive function; (3) teeth and coat color between four and seven years old, but the coat color must be one of three types: deer tail (date chestnut), chestnut (red hare), and dark (black); (4) body height from the withers to the ground must be more than four to five chi; (5) the head must be square, the forehead must be broad, the ears erect, and the eyes clear and spirited; (6) the body must be healthy, strong, and vigorous, with organ development, a shiny coat, and rich springiness; the temperament must be brave, lively, decisive, and intelligent. The show process was divided into three steps: first, looking at the physique; second, looking at the form; and finally, making an overall judgment.

The audience's attention was focused on the final day's final of pacing horses and running horses, so the stands and the outside of the track were crowded with spectators. Several famous jockeys had already become household names and were even more excited at this moment. Among them, the young children Li Ren and Yin Shixiang, who had won the championship in the previous year's competition and had been praised by Chairman Chiang, were the most prominent. It is said that when Chairman Chiang came to Suiyuan to watch the competition in the previous year, he saw that he was only a child of thirteen or fourteen years old, and he was able to win the championship in the running horse competition, so he awarded him 500 yuan and instructed Chairman Fu to cultivate him in school. The running horses in the final on the last day were all the horses that had won the semi-finals over the three days. They were truly "handsome horses, strong steeds." During the competition, the wind was blowing and the horses were galloping, and the crowd cheered. The atmosphere was tense, and it was truly exciting and emotional. In the end, Li Rong's Big Blue Horse from Baotou County took the lead with a time of two minutes, twenty-four and one-fifth seconds, winning the championship. Yin Shixiang, the young child who had attracted attention for days, was the runner-up because the horse's rein broke in the middle, and the horse's direction became unstable. After the final, Chairman Feng Xi and Chairman Fu of the conference committee gathered the first-place horses of each category to name them. The first-place colt was named "Dragon Colt," produced in Sazhou County; the first-place mule was named "Fankang," produced in Wuchuan County; the first-place pacing horse was named "Bian Cong," produced in the Central Public Banner of Mongolia; and the first-place running horse was named "Bei Ang," produced in Urad of Baotou. After the naming ceremony, an exhibition was held, with each first-place horse wearing a flower in its head, led by a military band to wait for the awards. The first-place winners each received a prize of 300 yuan and other prizes.

After the closing ceremony, the winning horses were led by a military band from the main road around the old city. At that time, the wide road was filled with flags and banners, the music was deafening, and the whole city was empty. Old and young came out to watch the excitement, which was crowded with people.

The results of this year's horse show were clearly better than those of the previous ones; especially the Mongolian horses participated more enthusiastically and were particularly excellent. However, the focus of the conference was on breed improvement, so special attention was paid to breed improvement methods after the conference.

In recent years, Suiyuan-produced horses can be sold to Guangdong and Guangxi, and even Gansu, which has always been known for its horse production, has come to buy them. This shows that sales are greater than before, and the central army sends people to Suiyuan to buy military horses every year, totaling several tens of thousands. This makes the people of Suiyuan who raise horses excited. It is said that the number of horses produced increased by about 10,000 last year. If the price of each horse is calculated at 50 yuan, then Suiyuan Province will invisibly increase its production by 500,000 yuan each year. This has a significant indirect impact on the welfare of the people in terms of finance. Therefore, this annual horse show can also be said to be an important task for the revitalization of the nation and economic construction. (Written in Saibei on October 13, 1936.)

Situation at the starting point of the running horse competition (Photo by Song Liangdong)

Chengdu Correspondence Chengdu and Chongqing (Part 1)

— Changqing

In Sichuan, Chengdu and Chongqing are two places that are quite famous, just like Nanjing and Shanghai in Jiangsu. However, if you were to ask some Sichuanese which province Chengdu and Chongqing belong to, they would be at a loss. It is not my intention to be deliberately sarcastic in describing them, but the prevalence of illiteracy in Sichuan—no, to put it more broadly, throughout China—is not surprising.

In terms of geographical situation, Chengdu relies on the mountains for its strength, with intricate water flows; Longquan (mountain name) and Minshan Mountains form a front and back barrier; the Min and Tuo Rivers surround the city, making it a naturally advantageous position, and it is an excellent place in the Sichuan Basin. Anyone who has been here knows that the land of the "West Sichuan Plain" is all black and oily, producing the largest amount of grain every year, which can not only supply the local people's food, but also export a large amount to the upper East Sichuan and North Sichuan regions. There are few floods and droughts, and famines like "eating the rich" are rare. Chongqing occupies the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, holding the throat of the entire province. Land and water transportation are accessible in all directions. It is a strategic location for military strategists, and the Tushan Zishui area has its own unique landscape!

Chengdu and Chongqing are more than a thousand kilometers apart. One is in West Sichuan, where the provincial capital is located, serving as the center of culture and politics. The other is in East Sichuan, the only important commercial port in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, where the province's economic power is concentrated and constantly rotating. Some have compared it this way: Chengdu is like present-day Beiping, while Chongqing is like Shanghai, only smaller. They are opposed to each other, but they also have a very close relationship.

"Go to Chengdu" or "Go to Chongqing." These are two common idioms for people from the interior of Sichuan when they go out. People who grew up in Sichuan have almost all heard these words to the point of nausea. These words clearly indicate the two important destinations for people who go out. Those who are used to "running around" focus their goals on these two places. Even some poor friends who have never gone out, if they are ever forced to develop outwards, their ideal places will inevitably be Chengdu and Chongqing.

Therefore, some people compare Chengdu and Chongqing to a pair of sisters; Chengdu is like a well-educated young lady from a wealthy family; Chongqing is like a vulgar and unbearable philistine woman. In the past, they were very incompatible. Since a string of cannons was fired from the other side of the Tuo River one year, they have reconciled. Now, from Chengdu to Chongqing, the waterway can go south through the Fujiang River, passing through Jiading, Jianwei, and Xufu before heading east. The land route relies only on the Chengdu-Chongqing Highway. Although there are other roads that can pass, they are all winding and dangerous. Therefore, even now, there still seems to be a layer of separation between Chengdu and Chongqing. If the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway is completed in the future, they will naturally become very close.

Because of historical and political relations, Chengdu is more culturally distinct. Emperor Liu Xian based himself here with a spirit of hard work; Zhang Xianzhong, who killed without batting an eye, once ruled as emperor in Chengdu; and some non-orthodox emperors and officials such as Meng Zhixiang and Wang Jian... all established their capitals here. Even now, the old site of the imperial city is still preserved. As for poets such as Du Fu and Xue Hongdu, the "globally renowned" female proofreader..., remnants and traces of their existence remain to this day, allowing people to mourn. Speaking of Chongqing, "Jiangba does not produce talented people," and no ancient emperor has ever favored it. It can be seen that the people lack cultural relics.

Current Affairs Commentary

National Funeral of Mr. Hu Zhantang

— The Capital

Today is the day of the national funeral for Mr. Hu Zhantang, Chairman of the Kuomintang Central Executive Committee, in Guangdong. The entire country is flying flags at half-mast and all forms of entertainment and banquets are suspended. In this solemn atmosphere, there is a deep sense of sorrow. This is to express the final farewell and mournful thoughts for this person who created the era. As the emotions are uniform, the actions will naturally be consistent. The central government had already dispatched personnel to prepare for the national funeral ceremony. The grandeur of the ceremony needs no further explanation, and the enthusiasm for participating in the memorial service is also the ultimate expression of honor and sorrow. The central government has already sent five members, including Ju Zheng and Sun Ke, to travel there promptly. Local authorities, organizations, and groups, both inside and outside the capital, have either sent representatives or individuals, all not shying away from the long journey. The sight of officials and dignitaries arriving in droves is imaginable. When we recall Mr. Hu's past merits and his integrity and self-discipline, his unyielding spirit, and our admiration for his noble character, our hearts are filled with emotions. We would also like to take this opportunity to express our condolences and profound admiration.

Mr. Zhantang passed away in Guangdong on May 12th of this year due to a cerebral hemorrhage. It has been five months and thirteen days since then. After the devastating news spread, the entire country expressed its shock and grief. The 12th meeting of the Central Executive Committee immediately resolved to hold a national funeral. Later, it was decided to appoint eleven people, including Xiao Focheng, as members of the preparatory committee for the national funeral ceremony. Initially, it was planned to relocate the burial to Nanjing. However, after accepting the family's proposal, Longyandong's Shiling Mountain in Panyu County was chosen as the burial site. The remains were originally placed in the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall. It was not until July 13th that they were moved to the Shiling Cemetery. The National Government issued an order on September 5th, designating October 25th as the date for the national funeral. After several careful deliberations and months of construction and preparation, the funeral arrangements have been completed. From now on, the tomb will be settled, and the spirit will be eternally at rest. As far as Mr. Hu is concerned, there should be no regrets. However, those who sincerely cared for Mr. Hu are saddened by the fact that his physical form is forever beyond reach, and they fear that the connection to his spirit will become increasingly distant. The feelings of bewilderment and sorrow are difficult to resolve. Fortunately, Mr. Hu's sincere words and clear teachings still resonate in our ears, providing guidance for reflection. Mr. Hu's steadfast integrity is engraved in our minds, providing ample inspiration. How to urgently catch up and implement his ideas is how we can comfort Mr. Hu, and not merely through funeral rites.

We have also read Mr. Hu's last instructions. Firstly, he said, "Political measures must be in accordance with the requirements of the country and the people." Secondly, he said, "The people of the whole country should use the spirit of resistance to protect the nation's survival to save the Chinese nation." Thirdly, he said, "What I deeply fear today is the ambiguity of national consciousness and the decline of national sentiment." Mr. Hu, aware of the imminent national crisis, deeply knew that without the power of national unity, there would be no hope of regeneration. Therefore, he repeatedly stated this to awaken attention. Tracing the purpose of his words, all the complex details can be summarized in one sentence: to cultivate a national renaissance movement. Unfortunately, Mr. Hu passed away with unfulfilled ambitions. How can we, the survivors, not continue his legacy? When commemorating Mr. Hu today, the people of the whole country should deeply recognize this point, constantly remind themselves, take it as their responsibility after death, and strive to achieve it.

Forty U.S. Navy Aircraft Conduct Exercises in the Central Pacific, Involving Over a Thousand Personnel, a Magnificent Spectacle Unprecedented in Air Force Maneuvers

Honolulu: Admiral King's flagship, the USS Wright, departed from Pearl Harbor today. Its destination is unknown. This is a signal for large-scale independent air force maneuvers to be held in the central Pacific. Four squadrons of U.S. Navy patrol aircraft will also depart from Pearl Harbor on Monday to participate in the exercises. The exercises will last for at least two weeks. These aircraft will use aircraft carriers as their base during the offensive and defensive war games and will concentrate near a certain shoal. The four squadrons of naval patrol aircraft, VP-1, VP-4, VP-8, and VP-10, consist of a total of forty aircraft, each with an average of five crew members. They will take off at dawn on Monday, led by Admiral King. The number of personnel participating in this exercise, including the eight hundred on board the flagship USS Wright and the crew of the twenty-three small steamers that departed with the flagship, will be over a thousand. The scope of the exercises and the number of aircraft and personnel involved are truly a magnificent spectacle unprecedented in air force exercises in the central Pacific. However, Admiral King is keeping the details of the exercises strictly confidential, only stating that they are routine exercises. The general area of the exercises is west of Midway Island, north of Wake Island, and south of Palmyra Island, but will also fly to Baker Island, Howland Island, and Jarvis Island. All of these are small coral islands in the Pacific that have recently been annexed by the United States. (National Telegram, 23rd)

British Export Department Representative to China Discusses Promoting Trade Again, Emphasizing the Need for Rapid Transportation, Expected to Arrive in China in Early December

(London) The newly appointed representative of the British Export Credits Guarantee Department to China, Mr. Kirkpatrick, gave an interview to the Daily Mail today, saying that British merchants must find ways to compete with American goods transported to China by fast ships and must strive to eliminate any disadvantages faced by Britain within the possible range. One issue that needs to be specially studied is the need to strive for the rapid transportation of passengers and goods. Mr. Kirkpatrick made the above remarks in response to a telegram sent by Lord Rothermere, the owner of a famous British newspaper, from Hong Kong, published in the Daily Mail, strongly urging the British government to provide assistance to British trade and shipping in the Far East.

U.S. Election Predictions: Roosevelt Likely to be Re-elected, Already Dominant in Thirty-Two States, Landon Only Confident in Sixteen States

(New York) According to comprehensive reports from Reuters reporters stationed throughout the United States, President Roosevelt is likely to win this election. Currently, Roosevelt is already dominant in thirty-two states, securing three hundred and fourteen electoral votes out of the five hundred and thirty-one electoral votes. The Republican presidential candidate, Landon, has a slight advantage in sixteen states, securing the remaining two hundred and seventeen electoral votes. (Note: The number of votes in each state is proportional to the number of its members in Congress.) The New England states, New York, and Pennsylvania have traditionally been Republican strongholds and are Landon's strong backing in this election, while the southwestern states all support President Roosevelt. Businessmen and financiers mostly support Landon, but organized labor and the unemployed all lean towards Roosevelt. The current debate is focused on President Roosevelt's personality and the achievements of the New Deal. Landon's attacks have mostly been ineffective. As for the power of the minor parties, it seems insignificant. (Reuters, 24th)

The leader of the Cooperative Party, Ji, although has the power to split the votes in Minnesota, is also extremely limited. Currently, the general election has reached its peak. Roosevelt is currently traveling in the East, while Landon is giving speeches in the West. It is reported that on the day before the election, the cost of radio broadcasts alone will reach 100,000 U.S. dollars. Landon's throat ailment has healed. He continued his speech in Oklahoma yesterday. Although his voice was slightly hoarse, speaking did not feel difficult. (Reuters, 24th)

(New York) The Literary Digest magazine released its near-final results of its public opinion survey for this year's presidential election today. Twelve states remain undecided between the Democratic and Republican parties: New York, Pennsylvania, Illinois, Ohio, Michigan, Minnesota, Wisconsin, Iowa, Indiana, Nebraska, Missouri, and West Virginia, accounting for 257 out of the nation's 531 electoral votes. Campaign leaders are all proclaiming victory, but all parties agree that the election is currently in a white-hot stage. Republican presidential candidate Landon has so far received 1,182,307 votes, corresponding to 370 electoral votes, with a lead in 32 states. President Roosevelt has received 878,526 votes, corresponding to 161 electoral votes, with a lead in the eleven southern states and Maryland, Kentucky, Oklahoma, New Mexico, and Utah. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) The White House announced today that President Roosevelt will depart from Washington at midnight on Tuesday to campaign in Pennsylvania, New Jersey, New York, and Delaware. On Wednesday morning, he will give a campaign speech in Bayonne and will take a boat to New York to attend the 50th anniversary celebration of the Statue of Liberty. On Thursday, the President will speak in Wilkes-Barre and then go to Harrisburg, Philadelphia, Camden, and Wilmington. This announcement has dispelled doubts that the President would be touring western states before the election. The President has returned from the industrial New England states today, confident that he can win the election. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) Today, the National Association of Manufacturers held dinners in eighteen locations. President Roosevelt delivered a radio address specifically for them. He dismissed the claim that the New Deal attempts to destroy private enterprise and establish socialism, saying that if the current government wanted to change the economic system, it could allow the old system to rot and harm the public. But we do not want to stand idly by and have decided to take active action to preserve private enterprise. The President also stated that business has improved considerably in recent days, but we should not cling to the theories of the prosperous era. The President concluded by declaring that he is determined to separate politics from business but also demands that business separate from politics, adding that the wage-earning class and the majority of businessmen are resentful of the few employers who spread rumors and deceive with alarmist statements. (National Telegram, 23rd)

(Washington) President Roosevelt delivered a speech here recently, advocating for the protection of private enterprise and accusing the financial world of harboring ambitions to regain control of industrial production and wealth distribution. He also said that the economic policies he is pursuing are between laissez-faire policies and various enterprise control policies. (Havas, 23rd)

Oklahoma: Republican presidential candidate Landon called on true Democrats and Republicans to join forces to oppose the New Deal, saying that the current government is not a democratic government. Landon praised the defection of important figures such as Al Smith, the Democratic presidential candidate in 1932. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Oklahoma: Republican presidential candidate Landon delivered a speech here today, criticizing President Roosevelt for destroying the political principles of the Democratic Party and calling on all true Democrats to unite with the Republican Party to "save the American political system." This is the first time that a Republican presidential candidate has openly sought the support of Democrats to jointly oppose Roosevelt's New Deal. (Havas, 23rd)

The Japanese Government Has Not Paid Up the Full Amount of South Manchuria Railway Shares, Matsuoka Asks Terauchi for Assistance, Tatekawa Reports His Impressions After the Inspection

(Tokyo) Matsuoka, President of the South Manchuria Railway, visited Army Minister Terauchi on the 24th, and Army Vice Minister Umezu was also present. They had detailed discussions for an hour and a half regarding the current state of the South Manchuria Railway's operations, the fourth railway construction plan, the issue of releasing all the shares of related business companies, and other matters, seeking the Army Minister's understanding. From the overall perspective of implementing the national policy towards Manchuria, he hoped for assistance. In particular, regarding the issue of the government's payment of share capital for its shares, President Matsuoka believed that this was not just a problem for the South Manchuria Railway but was also greatly related to the trends in the financial world, hoping that the government would actively proceed with it. The South Manchuria Railway is carrying out the plan of railway construction with great sacrifice and will continue to make the same efforts in the future. However, it seems that the authorities of the Ministry of Finance still do not understand the intentions of the South Manchuria Railway. He hoped that the Army Minister, in his capacity as Director-General of the Manchurian Affairs Bureau, would give it deep consideration. The Army Minister agreed with President Matsuoka's views and promised to provide assistance. (Domei, 24th)

Kobe: Lieutenant General Tatekawa arrived at Kobe port on the 24th morning aboard the Rehe Maru. According to him, although the situation on the Manchurian-Soviet border is tense, it is not considered to be on the verge of a sudden outbreak. He believes that the Soviet Union clearly harbors fear of the Japanese army, so it is striving to strengthen its military preparations. Manchurian immigrants have reached the realm of economic self-sufficiency and have achieved considerable success. However, the plan for one million households and 1.8 billion yuan over twenty years is still insufficient. Industrial development, especially heavy industry, has great potential in the future. Manchuria benefits from the 11 yuan tariff per ton on Japanese iron ore. To fully develop Manchuria, the current economic policy towards Manchuria is not sufficient. (Domei News Agency, 24th)

Japan Trains Flight Personnel, 500-600 Every Year

(Tokyo) In order to strengthen civil aviation, the Ministry of Communications has decided to train 100 aircraft operators every year, and the necessary expenses have been included in the next fiscal year's budget. Recently, it has further established a plan to train 500 student aviators every year. It will expand the organization of the Student Aviation League and build necessary facilities in cities such as Tokyo, Osaka, Nagoya, Sapporo, Sendai, and Fukuoka to conduct aviation training for 500 to 600 students. (Domei, 24th)

Our Country's Envoy to Czechoslovakia Presents Credentials

Prague: Liang Long, the newly appointed Chinese envoy to Czechoslovakia, presented his credentials to President Beneš today. The local press expressed its delight. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Spanish Rebel Army Aircraft Wreak Havoc, Aviator Freely Discusses Bombing Techniques, Apprehension Rises in the Capital

Madrid: Several rebel army aircraft dropped four bombs in the vicinity of Guadalajara today, causing great panic among the people in the capital. Yesterday, the Aranjuez radio station malfunctioned, disrupting telephone communication between here and London, but it has been restored today. It is said that the radio station may have been bombed by the rebel army. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Talavera: Although the troops of General Franco, Commander-in-Chief of the Spanish National Revolutionary Army, have temporarily halted their advance to consolidate their positions, their air force continues to attack day and night, greatly affecting the morale of the Madrid garrison and the trench defense fortifications of various key positions. The air force of the National Revolutionary Army possesses the latest type of aircraft, as can be proved by the conversation between a special correspondent of this newspaper and a member of the air force under General Franco today. According to the conversation, "We piloted the aircraft through the Guadarrama Mountains in the dark, then immediately shut off the engine so that there was no sound during the descent. In addition to machine guns, the aircraft was also equipped with magnesium bombs attached to parachutes, which emitted a bright light when dropped, making all the targets on the ground clearly visible. The aircraft I was piloting dropped four bombs with great explosive power, each weighing 250 kilograms. After that, the aircraft quickly ascended, making it impossible for anti-aircraft guns to use their skills." (Havas, 24th)

Madrid: The National Army announced in a communiqué that National Army aircraft bombed Bilbao Port in the northwest, Cartagena Port in the southeast, and the capital city yesterday. Two bombers belonging to the government army in the capital city were shot down. (Havas, 24th)

Casablanca: The Spanish government cruiser Libertad and two torpedo boats engaged the rebel cruiser Canarias in a chase in the Strait of Gibraltar today. The Canarias was heavily damaged by artillery fire, but it was able to safely escape to Ceuta in Morocco under the protection of two rebel army aircraft. The bow of the Libertad was also hit by a shell and, protected by two torpedo boats, sailed north. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Germany and Canada Sign Trade Agreement

(Berlin) The commercial and debt settlement agreement between Germany and Canada has been signed in Montreal, Canada, and will take effect on November 15. (National Telegram, 23rd)

Repeated European Crises, a Powder Keg About to Explode, Britain Purchases a Thousand Aircraft from the U.S., Causing Widespread Fear of War, Japan Pays Attention to the Development of the Situation

(New York) It is rumored that Britain is currently ordering 1,000 military aircraft from the United States and Canada, causing the stocks of aircraft manufacturing companies to soar today. It is reported that the Boeing Aircraft Manufacturing Plant in Canada will manufacture 300 bombers, and U.S. factories will manufacture 700 light bombers. The British people almost unanimously support the government's rearmament plan. Now, this development has increased people's fear of future wars. Some people now say that the capture of Madrid by the Spanish National Army will trigger a European war. Once the National Army enters the capital, Germany, Italy, Portugal, and Greece will recognize it as the legitimate government of Spain, and the United States will follow the lead of Britain and France. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Tokyo) Regarding the news that the Soviet Union has withdrawn from the Spanish non-intervention agreement and that the Portuguese government has severed diplomatic relations with Spain, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received official telegrams. As it has subtle implications for international relations, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is temporarily refraining from making any comments. In short, the movements of various countries tend to induce an intensification of the confrontation between the left and right wings in Europe. Therefore, special attention is paid to its progress. The statements of the Portuguese and Indian governments severing diplomatic relations with the Spanish government are also actions to counter the Soviet Union's support for the government army and to publicly clarify their stance of supporting the anti-government army. Therefore, the Soviet Union's resistance to Germany, Italy, and Portugal has intensified to the point of exercising its power at this time. The political situation in Europe has reached an unstable situation that is about to explode. However, Britain, in the midst of this, maintains a completely neutral stance. France, in view of the separation of the Little Entente countries, the rise of Germany, and the major changes in the international situation, has recently been changing to an ambiguous attitude of avoiding joint actions with the Soviet Union. Therefore, whether Britain and France can take effective measures to dissolve the imminent European war clouds is the most important factor in determining the future political trends, and thus it is particularly noteworthy. (Domei, 24th)

Manchester: Lloyd George, Prime Minister during World War I, declared to the Revival Movement Committee here today, "The current international situation has deteriorated, which has not happened since the Great War. If war is provoked by the intentional aggression of dictatorial countries, then the force in Europe against it is very strong, and it will never allow these countries to run rampant." (National Telegram, 23rd)

Soviet Russia Prepares for Free Action in Spain

(London) The Soviet government has now decided to resume its freedom of action regarding the issue of non-intervention in the Spanish civil war. However, for the time being, the Soviet representative will not withdraw from the Non-Intervention Committee. Today, the Soviet Ambassador to Britain, Maisky, wrote to the Chairman of the Adjustment Committee, Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs, Plymouth, saying, "The non-intervention agreement in the Spanish civil war has been repeatedly violated by several signatory countries. Portugal has virtually become a base for supplying the Spanish rebel army, while the legitimate government of Spain has been deprived of the convenience of purchasing military supplies from abroad to protect its people. This fact of violating the non-intervention agreement has created a superior position for the Spanish rebel army, resulting in the prolongation of the civil war in Spain and the increase in the number of victims. It seems that this non-intervention agreement is empty, becoming a piece of waste paper, and does not actually exist. Therefore, the Soviet government believes that the restrictions imposed on the Soviet Union regarding non-intervention in the Spanish civil war should not be greater than the restrictions imposed on any country that signed the non-intervention agreement." (Havas, 23rd)

(London) After the meeting of the Non-Intervention Committee, the Russian ambassador told a Reuters reporter that the Soviet Union had not formally withdrawn from the committee. Another Soviet representative said that the Soviet Union would still attend the subcommittee meeting held this morning. (Reuters, 24th)

(London) The subcommittee composed of thirteen representatives from major countries of the Non-Intervention Committee held a meeting at the British Foreign Office at 10:30 this morning to review the general work of the entire committee and asked the Soviet Union to clarify certain points in the letter from its Ambassador to the UK, Maisky, to the committee. Maisky arrived first. When a Reuters reporter asked if he thought the Soviet Union was bound by the letter, Maisky replied, "Yes, I think the letter takes effect when it is presented to the committee." The subcommittee met for two hours and forty-five minutes, considering whether the non-intervention agreement could be made more effective and, if so, by what means. It is said that no decisions were made, and discussions will continue early next week. (Reuters, 24th)

(Geneva) League of Nations officials predicted that if the Soviet government abandons the non-intervention agreement in the Spanish civil war, the League of Nations Council may convene a temporary meeting in the shortest possible time at the request of the Soviet government or the Madrid government. It is also said that the Soviet government's decision will definitely have serious implications, and the permanent delegations of the League of Nations member states are now closely monitoring the development of the situation. (Havas, 24th)

Committee Meeting

(London) The committee issued a communiqué stating that at the beginning of today's meeting, Lord Plymouth explained in detail that the British government agreed to set up a committee in London to prevent the Spanish civil war from spreading beyond its borders and to establish a cooperative plan for all countries to avoid the war from turning into an international crisis. He also urged all committee members to examine various intelligence with a spirit of fairness in order to fulfill their arduous work. Then, the letter from the Soviet Ambassador was officially read. After reading, the Portuguese representative stood up and firmly denied the Soviet Union's accusations of Portugal violating the agreement, dismissing them as unfounded. He said that it would be clear when Portugal's reply was received. The committee then decided to transfer the Soviet letter to the subcommittee and invited the Soviet representative to attend the meeting to clarify certain points in the letter. During the discussion, Lord Plymouth expressed his opinion, saying that the German government's reply to the Spanish government's accusations was very satisfactory, but there were only two points that needed to be further clarified by the German government. The committee then followed his suggestion and decided that the Soviet Union's proposal to have the British or French navy or the navies of both countries control Portuguese seaports could not be considered until Portugal's reply was received. The Portuguese representative declared that he could not agree to discuss the issue. The committee also decided that the subcommittee should meet tomorrow morning to review the general work of the committee and consider how to make the non-intervention agreement more effective. The Soviet Ambassador declared that he was willing to immediately reply to the rebuttals in the Italian and German replies, but the committee did not allow him to speak, saying that if he wanted to rebut, he should first submit a written text. Finally, the committee decided that the next meeting would be held on October 28. (Reuters, 23rd)

Portugal Announces Severance of Relations with Spain

Capital of Portugal: The Portuguese government has severed diplomatic relations with the Spanish government. Foreign Minister Mondero has presented a note to the Spanish Ambassador, Arboñez, explaining the reasons for this action. The full text will be released at an appropriate time. The Portuguese Chargé d'Affaires in Spain, Viscount Tamega, moved from Madrid to the port of Arigander in eastern Spain in August and has been ordered to board a Portuguese warship in that port and return home immediately. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

(Paris) Following the Portuguese government's severance of diplomatic relations with the Spanish government, political figures deeply fear that this will cause a serious reaction. It is believed that after Portugal's break with Madrid, Portugal, Italy, and Germany may recognize the National Army government in Burgos, Spain, in the short term. Thus, these three countries will regard the National Army government as the legitimate government of Spain, and subsequent supplies of arms to General Franco, the leader of the National Army government, may be considered legitimate. If so, some countries will recognize one government in Spain, while others will recognize another, creating a clear division and strict boundaries, and the international situation will become increasingly entangled and beyond repair. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

The True Intentions of Soviet Russia

(Moscow) The note delivered by Soviet Ambassador to the UK, Maisky, to the Non-Intervention Committee yesterday was worded ambiguously, causing considerable confusion among political figures here. However, it is generally expected that the Soviet Union is awaiting the reaction of various countries to this note. There is no doubt that the Soviet Union is willing to supply arms to the Spanish government, but it is also striving to avoid competition with Germany and Italy in transporting arms. Therefore, while the Soviet Union claims the right to act freely in Spain, it is unwilling to genuinely abandon the neutrality agreement, lest it be criticized by the world. The Soviet people are now prepared for any eventuality, but it is unlikely that there will be severe actions in the next few days. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

(London) The Supervisory Committee for the Non-Intervention Measures in the Spanish Civil War is scheduled to continue its meeting this afternoon. British Foreign Secretary Eden and the French Ambassador to the UK, Corbin, consulted this morning on how the non-intervention agreement can be effectively respected. It is reported that a plan has been decided upon, namely, that warships from each signatory country should be dispatched to monitor all Spanish ports, whether controlled by the government forces or the National Army. Although the Soviet Union has declared its willingness to withdraw from the committee, it still has a hidden desire to continue participating. This action by the UK and France is intended to satisfy this desire. Responsible parties have announced that this plan will be submitted for discussion at the meeting of the Supervisory Committee this afternoon, at which time the Soviet representative will also exert their strategy to the fullest extent. What is the strategy? It is to declare that the work of the Supervisory Committee has failed, so that world public opinion will sympathize with the Spanish government, thereby satisfying them. On the other hand, with the prospect of convening the Locarno Conference, the Soviet Union will certainly not want to withdraw from the international committee and thus become isolated. It is said that the reason why the Soviet Union has leveled accusations against certain countries for undermining the non-intervention agreement is driven by a desire to emulate the actions of those countries. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

(London) After the adjournment of the subcommittee of the Adjustment Committee for Non-Intervention Measures in the Spanish Civil War at 1:30 PM today, the Soviet representative, Chargé d'Affaires to the UK, Kagan, immediately declared that the Soviet delegation would continue to cooperate in the meetings of the Adjustment Committee for the time being. According to well-informed officials, the Soviet representative stated this morning in the subcommittee that he would inquire with Moscow about the meaning of the Soviet government's decision yesterday to resume free action on the issue of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War. At the same time, the British delegation is planning to propose that the countries concerned jointly dispatch warships to monitor Spanish ports, so as to satisfy the Soviet Union and provide a way to resolve the situation. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

Litvinov's Resignation is Untrue

(Moscow) Recent rumors in foreign newspapers that Litvinov will resign from his position as the People's Commissar for Foreign Affairs of the Soviet Union are completely unfounded. This is a malicious anti-Soviet rumor with no basis. (TASS Dispatch, 24th)

Spain Proves Again: Germany and Portugal Aid the Rebels - Three Italian Aircraft Arrive in Spain

(London) The Spanish government has sent two official documents to the British Foreign Office, listing various facts of violating the non-intervention agreement. The first document includes a photographic copy of a telegram from the Deputy Governor-General of Spanish Guinea, stating that the Portuguese ship "Macao," with its hull and smokestack painted in the German style, appeared outside the port at 8:00 AM on October 14. At close range, it shelled and sank the Spanish ship "Fernando Po," drowning the captain and 40 sailors. The Portuguese ship then shelled the Deputy Governor-General's residence, fortunately without hitting it. The second document states that on October 8, 160 German youths arrived in Seville on a German ship, carrying 12 anti-aircraft guns to join the rebels. On October 19, 16 German submarines sailed through the strait. On October 20, the German armored ship "Deutschland" sailed out of Malaga and Valencia, collecting orders and mail along the way to deliver to a German seaplane serving the rebels. Germany Announces Recognition of Italian Annexation of Abyssinia - Ciano Meets with Hitler: Results

(Berlin) Today, Germany has announced its formal recognition of the Italian East African Empire, including Abyssinia. This is the first concrete result after Foreign Minister Ciano's visit to Berlin. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

(Berlin) A spokesman for the German Foreign Ministry declared today that Germany's recognition of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia was not conditional on any concessions from the Italian side. It should be known that this situation is a natural result, as Germany has always maintained a neutral policy and strives to avoid being drawn into any conflict that has nothing to do with Germany. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

Berchtesgaden: Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano arrived here from Berlin by special train at 9:00 AM today. He immediately traveled by car to the villa of Führer Hitler, where he held talks with Hitler and Foreign Minister Neurath. At 1:00 PM, they had lunch together in the villa, and the talks continued uninterrupted until 3:00 PM. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

(Berlin) After Führer Hitler, accompanied by Foreign Minister Neurath, received Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano at his villa in Berchtesgaden this morning, an official communiqué was immediately issued, stating: "Führer Hitler has just announced to the foreign ministers of Italy and Germany that Germany now formally recognizes Abyssinia as part of the Italian Empire. Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano immediately expressed that the Italian Fascist government is extremely pleased with this action by Germany."

Siena: Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano arrived here from Berchtesgaden at 4:50 PM today. The authorities of the province of Pavia and members of the National Socialist Party welcomed him at the station. Flags were flying throughout the city, and posters were posted everywhere, informing residents that they should stand on both sides of the streets passed by Ciano to express their welcome. Ciano then inspected the National Socialist stormtroopers and members of the Fascist Party in the city and is scheduled to visit the National Socialist Party headquarters this evening. He will also attend a dance party and listen to performances of works by the famous Austrian composer Mozart and the Italian composer Donizetti at the opera house. At 9:00 AM tomorrow, he will meet with journalists and issue a final communiqué. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

(Berlin) Italian Foreign Minister Ciano set off this evening for Berchtesgaden in the province of Bavaria to pay his respects to Führer Hitler and hold talks. The journey will take him through Mingnon before he can reach the destination. Those traveling with Ciano include German Foreign Minister Neurath, Director of Political Affairs of the Chancellery Lammers, Director of Protocol of the Foreign Ministry Schwendemann, German Ambassador to Italy Hassel, and members of Ciano's staff. It is clear that the real meeting between Italy and Germany will be held in Berchtesgaden. (Havas Dispatch, 33rd [likely an error in the original text])

(Berlin) Italian Foreign Minister Ciano and German Foreign Minister Neurath have been negotiating the Spanish situation and general European issues for days and are about to reach an agreement. The key lies in the meeting between Ciano and Führer Hitler tomorrow. After the meeting, a statement will be issued announcing the views of Italy and Germany on European issues. It is believed here today that Germany and Italy will not sign any formal treaty, at least not before Ciano returns home to report to Prime Minister Mussolini. (National Dispatch, 23rd)

Germany Prepares: Goering Orders Control of Industry

(Berlin) Minister of Aviation and Prussian Prime Minister General Goering was recently appointed as the dictator of the four-year economic plan. To ensure that German industry is fully prepared, he ordered today the implementation of control over the entire national industry, making it "more complete than in wartime." A committee composed of ministers from various departments related to economic recovery will implement this plan. The committee will be divided into six major departments, responsible for production, raw material allocation, labor, agriculture, and financial issues. (National Dispatch, 23rd)

(Berlin) After being appointed as the dictator of the four-year plan, Minister of Aviation and Prussian Governor General Goering yesterday appointed Lieutenant Colonel Robber as "Director of the German Raw Materials Production Division." Although the details of the four-year plan are not known to outsiders, the fact that Lieutenant Colonel Robber has been appointed as the director with a military background shows that military supplies and military issues must occupy a primary position in this plan. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

British King Reviews Navy

(London) According to a statement from the Admiralty, King Edward will travel to the waters off Portland on November 23 aboard the Royal Yacht to review the Home Fleet. He will be accompanied by officers such as Naval Secretary Sir Hoare. This is the first review of the Home Fleet by the King since his ascension to the throne. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

French Radical Party: Cooperation with the Communist Party - Heated Debate Begins at Congress

Biarritz: A resolution of great importance to the life of the Socialist Party government led by incumbent Prime Minister Blum is being hotly debated at the Radical Party Socialist Congress here. The focus of the issue is whether to continue cooperation with the Communist Party. The current situation has become quite dark due to the attitude taken by the Soviet Union yesterday towards non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War. Blum's future is difficult to be optimistic about. At yesterday's congress, Radical Party Socialist leader Herriot made a shocking request, advocating continued cooperation with the Communist Party, but after the news that the Soviet Union had effectively withdrawn from the non-intervention agreement, Herriot's request has been implicitly dismissed. (Reuters Dispatch, 24th)

Biarritz: The Radical Socialist Congress is scheduled to continue its meeting this afternoon to begin discussing general political issues. At that time, the two factions supporting and opposing the People's Front will engage in fierce verbal battles to determine the final outcome. Four proposals will be submitted at today's meeting: (1) The proposal submitted by Roche, leader of the Radical Socialist branch in the Northern Province; (2) The proposal submitted by Radical Socialist member Tauminique. The above two proposals both support continued participation in the People's Front, but with the condition that the Communist Party must provide a definite guarantee not to restrain the government's actions. (3) The proposal of Radical Socialist Congressman Kaiser. This proposal has been approved by 40 branches of the Radical Socialist Party, advocating that the party continue to participate in the People's Front and remain loyal to the current government, but demanding that law and order be maintained and that the occupation of factories by workers be stopped. The Radical Socialist member Beyer's proposal expresses trust in the People's Front and opposes all cabinet organizations that violate the wishes of the voters in the last general election. The proponents of the above proposals, as well as former Interior Minister Marchandeau-Gruneau, former Commerce Minister Pommier, etc., will all deliver speeches this afternoon. Defense Minister Daladier will also speak, so that a common resolution can be passed unanimously, using Kaiser's proposal as its blueprint. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

Biarritz: The drafting committee of the Radical Socialist Congress convened this afternoon at 3:00 PM and began drafting a resolution for the congress. The task was completed at 8:00 PM. This resolution will be submitted to the congress in the name of the majority faction of the Radical Socialist Party. Its content approves the party's cooperation with the current government and advocates demanding that the current government respect the party's major principles within its platform. Another minority of Radical Socialists, led by Roche, leader of the Northern Province branch, intends to submit another motion targeting the actions of the Communist Party, which is worded more strongly. The above two drafts will be publicly submitted for discussion tomorrow, at which time the situation will be extremely heated. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)

Belgian Right-Wing to Hold Major Demonstration Today

The Hague: The fascist Rexist Party, disregarding the government's ban, has decided to hold a demonstration tomorrow. To prevent any unforeseen circumstances, the government has taken precautionary measures. It is believed that no serious conflicts will occur. According to the party's agreed plan, all members were originally intended to gather in a private residence in the suburbs. It is now heard that this plan has been abandoned, and they plan to take the opportunity to join the ranks of the veterans of the Battle of the Yser in World War I when they parade in front of King Leopold III at 10:00 AM tomorrow. This plan has also been detected by the government, so it has ordered the veterans to shorten the ranks to avoid being exploited, even if the veterans are disappointed and unhappy. Therefore, the party leader has now changed the plan again, intending to immediately notify party members to gather at noon tomorrow, but the location of the gathering has not been announced. The entire city's military police have now been ordered to board and inspect all cars arriving in the capital from the provinces, especially those carrying many passengers. However, how many party members from the provinces who have obeyed the party headquarters' orders and come to the capital is still unknown to the party leaders at this moment. The party leader Degrelle told our reporter, "Our party intends to show the whole country its wishes. What are the wishes? That energetic, morally integrated, and patriotic people should hold official positions, while other mad dogs with revolutionary ideas should be sent to Moscow. As far as my announcement is concerned, all acts of violence are prohibited." Degrelle also said that in addition to holding a demonstration tomorrow, the party will also hold nine mass demonstrations across the country on November 1, including major cities such as Brussels, Antwerp, Liège, and Ghent. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

International Labour Maritime Conference Passes Draft Conventions

(Geneva) The International Labour Office Maritime Conference passed five draft conventions this morning: (1) The draft convention on certificates of competency for shipmasters was passed by a majority of 80 votes to 9. (2) The draft convention providing for 12 days of annual leave for ship officers and 9 days of annual leave for seafarers was passed by a majority of 60 votes to 15. (3) Two draft conventions on seafarers' sickness insurance, one passed by a majority of 70 votes to 14 and the other by a majority of 60 votes to 6. (4) The draft convention on employing seafarers on ships of 2,000 tons or more for 56 hours per week was passed by a majority of 62 votes to 17. Representatives of the British and Japanese governments both voted against it. (5) Two recommendations, one advocating that the minimum age for working as a seafarer be increased from 14 to 15 years old, and the other advocating improving the living conditions of seafarers in various ports. (Havas Dispatch, 24th)

(Geneva) The International Labour Office Maritime Conference continued its meeting today to discuss the draft convention on seafarers' working hours. The Chinese government representative, Bao Huaguo, made a declaration stating that the Chinese government, in principle, supports the eight-hour day system for seafarers. However, the convention on seafarers' working hours only applies to ocean-going vessels, and the Chinese shipping industry currently lacks such vessels. Therefore, the Chinese government cannot ratify this draft convention in the near future. However, to express the Chinese government's support for the principle of eight-hour work, it will vote in favor of this draft convention. Thereupon, the Maritime Conference passed the draft convention on seafarers' working hours on first reading. The draft convention stipulates that, in principle, employees on ships of 2,000 tons or more should work 56 hours per week. When the draft convention was put to a vote, the British government representative, Jenkins, stated that he was instructed by his government to vote against the draft convention and said that the British government did not intend to ratify this convention. Subsequently, the Chinese labor representative, Zhao Banfu, submitted two resolutions: (1) requesting the Governing Body of the International Labour Office to discuss the issue of equal treatment for domestic and foreign seafarers; (2) demanding the abolition of the foreman contracting system. The so-called foreman contracting system is where the foreman contracts to hire workers, thus depriving seafarers of their freedom to choose ships, and hired seafarers are often subjected to inhumane treatment, so it should be abandoned urgently. These two resolutions were passed by the Maritime Conference and submitted to the Governing Body of the International Labour Office for handling. The Maritime Conference then passed a proposal by Japanese seafarer representative Horiuchi, advocating that the issue of compensation for seafarers injured on duty be discussed at the next Maritime Conference. Finally, the Maritime Conference passed a joint proposal by Japanese seafarer representative Horiuchi and employer representative Kawakawa, stating that the Maritime Conference supports finding ways to convene a world economic conference to promote economic recovery, so that the transportation industries of various countries in the world can be restored to prosperity. (Havas Dispatch, 23rd)
