The Jianghai Customs issued a notice to merchants to bid for sugar goods: This Customs now has 12 bags of sugar cubes, weighing 565 kilograms, 130 bags of crystal sugar, weighing 28,485 kilograms, 80 bags of fine white sugar, weighing 2,070 kilograms, and 1,626 bags of white sugar, weighing 50,000 kilograms. They are currently stored in the Customs Pudong Warehouse and are being tendered for sale. The weight of these items are all approximate figures and can be accurately weighed during delivery. During the tender period, from 9:00 am to 4:30 pm every day, merchants can apply to the Transportation Department of this Customs to inspect the goods and extract samples. The letter can specify the purchase of all or only part of the goods. It must be submitted to the Taxation Department of the General Affairs Section of this Customs before 10:00 am on Wednesday, October 28th of this year. This Customs reserves the right not to accept the highest bid or any tender. The successful bidder shall submit 25% of the bid price to the Customs on the same day and pay for the goods and take delivery within one week. This is hereby announced.

Public Concession - Health Conditions Last Month - Vaccination Work Actively Carried Out - Increase in Malaria is Alarming

According to the Public Works Department's health report for September, the mortality rate of Chinese and foreign residents in the Concession this month, although above the normal level, has no special symptoms in terms of diseases. Regarding infectious diseases, the occasional outbreak of smallpox is extremely worrying. Now that the free vaccination provided by the Health Department is very convenient, residents in the Concession who have not been vaccinated or have been vaccinated for a long time should go for vaccination as soon as possible, especially those who have recently come to Shanghai from other places. Otherwise, the consequences will be unimaginable. Furthermore, malaria in this port is now becoming more and more rampant, which is an alarming phenomenon. According to the report in June of this year, the number of people with malaria in the Concession was only 32. In July, it increased to 96. In August, it increased to 157. And the number of reported malaria cases in September reached 206. The source of this disease is nothing more than infection through travel to malaria-prone areas. Furthermore, the cholera prevention work this year ended at the end of this month, and the staff have also been transferred to vaccination work. According to statistics, a total of 124,043 people were vaccinated this year, and 31,933 people received the second injection. It is fortunate that cholera has not occurred this year. In addition, notable diseases include 120 cases of dysentery and 17 cases of typhoid fever. Regarding rabies, two people died in September, a British child of 16 years old and a Chinese man. Both died without timely treatment. Furthermore, there are many blood flukes in the ponds and banks in the suburbs of Shanghai. The Health Department has repeatedly issued warnings before, but unfortunately, residents and Boy Scouts who camp in the suburbs do not pay attention to this, resulting in many people being infected with blood fluke disease after returning. They should be treated quickly, otherwise it will be too late.

###诱惑(誘惑)妇人(婦人)诈骗(詐騙)巨金(鉅金) - Ye Fook Hon Accused - Wang Hon Hing States Ye's Methods too Vicious - Lists Facts to Accuse Department of Justice - Court Summons Lawyer Fan Gong to Testify

Ye Fook Hon, who served as a candidate judge in the criminal court of the Shanghai Local Court in 1927, is a native of Wujiang, Jiangsu Province. Later, because he was hearing a case in which the Taicang County Party Department reported local tyrants and evil gentry Yao Heling, Ye mistakenly cited the law and did not handle it in accordance with the law on punishing local tyrants and evil gentry, and detained the reporter Cao Runtang, a party committee member, for false accusation. Therefore, he was disciplined by the Central Party Department. As a result, the former President Yang Zhaoyun was given a major demerit, and Ye was dismissed. In May 1928, he joined the Shanghai Lawyers Association to practice as a lawyer. His residence number is 1311 Yiwangjiazhai, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. He has the most law offices and branch offices. In recent years, he has also created four Little Luzon hat shops, becoming a famous lawyer and a famous new business merchant in Shanghai. Recently, Wang Hon Hing accused Ye Fook Hon in the Department of Judicial Administration of defrauding him of his huge family wealth and seducing his wife. According to Wang Hon Hing, when Wang was implicated in a theft case in 1931, he had already hired lawyer Fan Gong to defend him and had paid a public fee of 1,500 yuan. However, this was known to his lawyer's broker, who brought Wang's wife to lawyer Ye's office and said that 10,000 yuan could guarantee that he would be declared innocent. At that time, he was trapped in error. Ye formally wrote to lawyer Fan Gong's office and transferred all the documents to Ye for handling. As a result, Wang Hon Hing was sentenced to one year and six months in prison. In the middle, due to appeals, he was detained for two or three years. However, Ye defrauded money by taking advantage of his position and coveted Wang's wealth. Wang's wife was young and could be deceived, so she was seduced and became an adulteress, cohabiting for a long time. As a result, the huge wealth of tens of thousands of dollars was all transferred away, so his property was used for his Little Luzon hat shop career. But when Wang's prison term was about to expire, Ye ordered Wang's wife to separate from Wang. When Wang's wife asked for huge sums of money, Ye said that it had been used up during the cohabitation and would not return it. However, at the beginning of Wang's imprisonment, 15 gold bars were found in his house during a search. It was found that they were not stolen goods and were returned to Wang. However, Ye colluded with many people to threaten him, demanding that they share the gold bars, otherwise they would find someone to report to the authorities that they were stolen in another case. Wang was threatened and listened to their arrangements to swallow seven or eight tenths of the gold bars. Therefore, because the methods were too vicious, he filed a complaint with the Department of Judicial Administration and would have his wife file a separate complaint. It is now found that this case was previously investigated by the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate under the direction of the Department of Judicial Administration. Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu ordered Ye Mao Kang to pay 20,000 yuan in bail and released him on the spot. In the past few days, according to Wang Hon Hing's lawsuit, someone had mediated. The court had summoned lawyer Fan Gong, lawyer Gu Ao, lawyer Zha Renwei, and lawyer Shen to testify.

Nanyang Tobacco Company - Minutes of Yesterday's Shareholders Meeting

The meeting began at 2:00 pm as scheduled. Chairman Chen Bingqian presided over the meeting and reported on the company's operating situation for the year. Then, Supervisor Lao Zesheng read the 16th annual financial report. There were no objections. Then, the Chairman proposed a vote to elect directors and supervisors. Shareholders Wang Wendian and others publicly elected Zhuang Zikuan and Wang Junzhi as tellers. Wang Junzhi publicly elected Zhou Qingquan and Wang Wendian as supervisors to open the ballots. As a result of the ballot opening, the most elected directors were: Jian Kongzhao, Pan Xingnong, Jian Yujie, Jian Minxuan, Zhou Shouchang, Du Yuesheng, Song Ziliang, Lao Jingxiu, Feng Bingnan, Chen Bingqian, Lu Yunqiu, Jian Yingfu, Jian Chengwan, Jian Zhichuan, and Pan Yucun. The most elected supervisors were Lao Zesheng and Chen Jizhi. The next most elected alternate supervisors were Liang Ziyu and Li Zhongguang. The results were announced on the spot, and the meeting was adjourned with the ringing of a bell.

National Assembly Hall - Construction Project Completed - Lu Genquan Talks About the Construction Process

Lu Genquan, the owner of the Lu Genji Construction Company, which contracted to build the National Assembly Hall, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday and told reporters from the Architecture News Agency that he (Lu referred to himself) had won the bid at the end of November last year to contract the construction of the National Art Exhibition Hall and the National Academy of Drama and Music, with a construction cost of 378,000 yuan. Later, because the Art Exhibition Hall added a floor and the Academy of Music added cold and hot gas pipe trenches, sub-road excavation, and Yinming trenches, another 300,000 yuan was added, so the total construction cost was 678,000 yuan. Other projects added from time to time are not included. On November 29th of the same year, the preparatory committee Chuminyi, Zhang Daofan, Chen Shuren, Chen Lifu, and others presided over the groundbreaking ceremony. Dean Ju presided over the ceremony. Drama artists who participated in the ceremony on that day included Tian Han, Hong Shen, Ouyang Yuqian, Tang Huaiqiu, Ying Yunwei, and more than 30 others. After the groundbreaking, the work was completely suspended from February to the end of April due to repeated changes in the drawings and other reasons. Then, Chuminyi, the director of the preparatory committee, received a thunderous order from Chairman Jiang, approving the renaming of the National Academy of Drama and Music to the National Assembly Hall, to be used as the venue for this National Assembly. In mid-April of this year, the Preparatory Committee renamed architect Fan Wenzhao as consulting architect, and Commissioner Chu personally inspected the site three to five times a day. The construction became increasingly tense, and he also stayed in the factory to facilitate command and easy response. During the construction period, National Government Chairman Lin, Dean Ju, Dean Sun, Minister Kong, and Wu Zhi Lao all visited the site and gave instructions. On August 10th, the Preparatory Committee received a letter stating that the date of the General Assembly had been decided and that it was of great importance to the whole country. There could be no delay, so the construction project must be completed on schedule. It was necessary to plan comprehensively, take effective measures, speed up construction, and complete the project on schedule to avoid delaying the opening date. It was a major national ceremony and should not be violated, causing inconvenience. Chen Shuren of the Preparatory Committee repeatedly limited the completion date to the end of October. Therefore, electric lights were installed throughout the factory, and more than a thousand workers worked day and night. He forgot to sleep and eat for more than ten days. During this period, he flew to Shanghai for medical treatment for about a week due to illness. The efforts of Mr. Chen, the general supervisor of the factory, during this period should not be ignored. For the sake of safety, the Preparatory Committee temporarily hired 1,500 workers on the 16th to conduct a pressure test on the stands, which was presided over by architect Fan Wenzhao, who came to Beijing. The results were good. Chairman Lin also came to the site for inspection. At present, the internal painting project has been completed one after another and is expected to be completed on schedule by the end of this month and handed over to the Preparatory Committee for acceptance and management. The Art Exhibition Hall and the National Assembly Hall are both three-dimensional buildings, towering on the side of the National Government Road, which is extremely spectacular. There is a modern stage in the Assembly Hall, which can seat 1,800 people upstairs and 1,000 people in the stalls. The three floors can seat 600 people. The front stage is four stories high, and the back stage is eight stories high, which can fully accommodate all great scenery and props. In short, he spent a lot of money on materials for the construction of the National Assembly Hall this time due to the limited completion date, and suffered great losses in construction. All sacrifices were made at all costs. Although the General Assembly was announced to be postponed, the construction of the Assembly Hall was finally completed on schedule, so he felt much comforted in spirit. It is said that Mr. Lu will stay in Shanghai for a few days and will go to Beijing to start the procedures for the transfer of the new building to the committee.

Municipal Health Bureau - Bans Unlicensed Female Doctors

The baby daughter of Zhou Xiangfan, a resident of No. 7 Zhangjia Muqiao, Pengpu District, Zhabei, was only a month old. She hired Yang Zhang, a neighbor, to treat her oral disease. Yang Zhang claimed that it was "螳螂子(Tanglangzi, Mantis offspring)", and used a knife to perform surgery in her mouth, causing blood to flow like a flood. She died soon after. Zhou Xiangfan immediately took Yang Zhang to the Xinza Public Security Bureau and filed a complaint with the Health Bureau, requesting that she be investigated and punished according to law. After receiving the report, the bureau sent staff to investigate and found that the facts were true. It was also found that Yang Zhang was an ignorant woman who dared to practice medicine without a license and harm people's lives. This was extremely illegal. It sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau to send her to the court for strict handling. It is said that the bureau has recently sent staff to conduct on-site investigations and strictly ban unlicensed quacks in the city to maintain the health of citizens.

Children's Supplement of Shen Bao, Boy Scouts

Meaning

Little brothers and sisters, when you reach the fifth or sixth grade in school, you will become Boy Scouts. I feel very happy about this.

Why am I happy to see you become Boy Scouts? It is because I think you look mighty and brave in your Boy Scout uniforms, which can represent a new spirit of China!

Recalling when I was your age, I didn't enjoy such happiness. There were no Boy Scouts then. We didn't wear such solemn uniforms like you do, and we couldn't show the spirit of vigor and bravery.

Boy Scout training is to make you lively, brave, and loving, to practice the skills and knowledge necessary for life, to teach you how to cook and camp, to teach you to "do a good deed every day," and to teach you to "act bravely for righteousness." Before the widespread organization of Boy Scouts, this kind of training could only be learned from textbooks, but it is indeed a very meaningful training. It is really a good phenomenon that it can be widely implemented now.

Little brothers and sisters, I hope that after you become Boy Scouts, you will get many benefits and be able to help yourselves, help others, and help the country!

Random Chats on Children's Stories By Yi Sheng

Wei Jie Asks About Dreams

Wei Jie was a famous handsome man. When he walked on the road, many women would rush to look at his face, so there was an idiom at the time, "Watching Wei Jie to Death." He was not only beautiful but also talented and had been studying hard since he was a child. When his hair could just be tied up, he was extremely suspicious of the reasoning behind dreams and was unwilling to let it go so casually like ordinary children, so he asked Mr. Le Guang. Mr. Le explained, "Dreams are formed by thoughts." Wei Jie asked again, "Things that the spirit and body have never come into contact with also enter dreams. Does that also come from thoughts?" Mr. Le said, "That always has a cause. No one has ever dreamed of riding in a car but going into a rat's hole, or grinding vegetables but chewing a pestle, because there is no such thought or cause." Wei Jie respectfully took his leave and went home, pondering all day long, "What is called cause?" His small brain overworked, and he became sick from excessive thinking. Mr. Le learned of the situation and quickly went to his house by carriage, explaining and analyzing it to him in great detail. His illness subsided quickly. Mr. Le couldn't help but praise, "This child's heart should not develop diseases of stagnation—where something remains and obstructs the middle, causing illness!"

Confucius taught us, "If in doubt, ask." This is really the initial step in learning and cannot be neglected in the slightest! But unfortunately, there are not many children who are willing to ask now, and even after asking, they still may not fully understand. Very few are willing to repeatedly ask their teachers for instruction! This situation is caused by three reasons: one is the habit of laziness, not seeking thorough understanding in everything, and not asking at all; another is pretending to be smart, fearing that asking again will make their peers look down on their natural talent; and the third is retreating in the face of difficulty, fearing that continuing to ask may not lead to sudden enlightenment but will instead annoy the teachers and be reflected in their expressions. If any of these three apply, children will not be able to "know when they know, and admit when they do not know." This relies on the enlightenment and skillful guidance of teachers and elders, in my opinion.

Xi'er's Awakening By Fang Zheng

Zhong'er and Xi'er are two brothers who study at ×× School. They not only have a spirit of mutual respect and love but also have unity! Occasionally, when someone bullies them, they immediately unite to give the bully a good beating! So, we can truly praise them with a saying: "Brotherly love"!

However, since Jing'er, nicknamed Short Winter Melon, came to their second grade class last year, their relationship has gradually faded. Because Short Winter Melon, although young, is really a bad kid. He can say to Zhong'er, "Xi'er is scolding you!" But at the same time, he can say to Xi'er, "Zhong'er is saying bad things about you!" After his instigation, the most loving brothers have to turn into strangers and enemies, and they even quarrel with each other relentlessly. But Short Winter Melon watches it as a play, secretly laughing. Sometimes, he even brags among his classmates about how strong his instigating skills are!

One day, he instigated Xi'er to steal Zhong'er's fountain pen to lend to him. But Xi'er, being ignorant, finally fell for his trick. The next day in class, Zhong'er discovered that his fountain pen was gone and searched everywhere but couldn't find it. So, he told the teacher, who, after investigating, found it in Short Winter Melon's bag. Everyone thought that this bad egg must have stolen it, so they insisted that the teacher expel him. But unexpectedly, Short Winter Melon calmly told the teacher the reason why Xi'er lent it to him and how Xi'er stole it. He also returned the fountain pen to Xi'er in front of everyone. In this way, Short Winter Melon was not only not expelled but Xi'er was also lectured by the teacher.

When Xi'er returned home, he pondered how to face his brother and parents. "I should wake up and realize that I fell for someone else's trick." So, he immediately apologized to his brother. On the other hand, he made an oath with Zhong'er: "Never associate with Short Winter Melon, restore our inherent unity, and defeat our enemies. We must know that brotherly discord is enough to destroy everything!"

Little friends! What are your thoughts after reading this?

The Story of the Horse By Ouyang Hui

A long, long time ago, in the shaded avenues of the forest, a group of free horses were all sighing and saying, "Why are we always bullied by those horned devils—the deer? Can't we really resist them??" But they ultimately had no strength to resist the deer because, upon seeing them, their hearts would thump, all resistance would be lost, and they would flee with their tails drooping. One day, the horses were strolling outside the forest when they encountered two hunters. They had a desire for revenge and, in a very pitiful manner, told the hunters and begged them to avenge them. The hunters readily agreed. So, they knelt down and allowed the hunters to ride on their backs, leading them to the enemies' location. The hunters then drove away and stabbed the deer to death. The two horses, seeing that their great revenge had been taken, thought they could finally relax and happily wanted to bid farewell to the hunters and return. But the hunters said with cold smiles, "Huh! It's not that easy! We still need you!" They took two thick ropes and, without any politeness, led the two horses into this harsh world.

Children's Free Book

The Biggest Flower and the Smallest Bird By Mingxin

Little friends, aren't the flowers we usually see only as big as our palms? But in the Philippines, there is a peculiar plant that has what can be considered the largest flower in the world. When it is in full bloom, it is more than three feet in diameter—about the size of a small peach tree. Can't that be considered the largest flower?

Little friends probably already know that the pollen from the stamens of a plant's flower must be transferred to the pistil for fruit to form. Pollen transferred by water is called water-pollination; pollen transferred by wind is called wind-pollination; pollen transferred by insects such as bees, butterflies, and moths is called insect-pollination; and some plants are pollinated by bats or snails. But in tropical America, there is a small bird that can also pollinate, called bird-pollination. This bird is light and small, only a little over ten centimeters in size, about the size of half a newspaper, and weighs about the same as a bee, so people call it a hummingbird. The hummingbird can be considered the smallest bird in the world. The hummingbird's beak is very slender, making it easy to suck nectar. Its colors are very beautiful, with bright emerald green feathers on its back and red and shiny down on its throat, chest, and abdomen. Its voice is very clear. It lives in dense small leaves, and its nest is built very skillfully. It often flies back and forth in the flowers like bees and butterflies, using its slender beak to reach into the flowers and suck the sweetness. Sometimes it also catches small harmful insects to eat. When it stretches its beak into the flower to suck nectar, it unintentionally scatters the pollen on the feathers of its long beak and transfers it to other flowers.

Children's Creation

Two Classmates Who Loved Eating Snacks By Cao Meiying, Fourth Grade Girl, Wan Zhu Elementary School

Among my classmates, there is a girl named Yin. Her family is also very wealthy, so her pockets are often full of money. However, in school, she doesn't study very hard, but she is very particular about snacks. Every day after arriving at school, she only likes to buy snacks to eat. One day in the morning, I saw her buy two pieces of bread and some beef. Before long, she had eaten them all up. After two classes, the things she had eaten started to act up, and she suddenly had a stomachache. She asked the teacher for leave to go home. Unexpectedly, she was sick for more than a month, abandoning her studies, and she was afraid that she would not be able to advance to the next grade this semester.

Among the classmates, there is a boy named Zhang, about thirteen or fourteen years old, who studies very hard. His family is wealthier than mine, so his pockets are also often full of money. I really don't understand why he often has a toothache. Later, after I inquired from other classmates, I learned that he only likes to buy snacks to eat. Among the snacks, he especially likes eating preserves, such as Gong Sheng Sugar, eggplant coffee sugar, and other fragrant and dry things. Last Monday, he took leave due to toothache and has been out for more than a week. His grades for the next semester will inevitably be affected.

Now I am writing about my classmates and submitting this as a contribution without any malice. If classmates Yin and Zhang didn't like eating snacks, they probably wouldn't have so many illnesses, and they wouldn't waste money. I hope that all the children in the country will not buy too many snacks to eat.

Scientific Little Question

Why is the Water in a Thermos Not Easily Cooled? By Zixi

Anyone who has used a thermos knows that it is not easy to cool down the hot water stored inside. Before I explain the reason, let me talk about a few things related to heat: heat is a form of energy, and it will never be destroyed in the universe. However, it always flows from substances with higher temperatures to substances with lower temperatures. Here, there are four ways of dissipating heat: radiation, convection, evaporation, and conduction. After we understand these causes of heat loss, let's examine the structure of a thermos: a thermos can be divided into two parts: one is the glass flask, and the other is the metal casing. The flask is made of a double-walled glass bottle, and there is a gap in between. The opposing glass walls in the gap are coated with a layer of silver. When the flask is first made, a solution containing silver is poured into the gap. When the silver is deposited on the two glass surfaces, the remaining solution is poured out, and then a vacuum pump is used to completely extract the air from the gap, making it a complete vacuum. Finally, the air extraction port is sealed. As for the outer casing, it is originally for protecting the flask and making it easier to carry. The reason why the water in a thermos is not easily cooled is that a vacuum can prevent heat conduction; radiant heat is reflected back by the silver layer on the glass walls; and the wooden stopper at the mouth prevents convection and evaporation. With these reasons, it is naturally easy to understand why the hot water in a thermos does not cool down easily.

Famous Things in the World (1) By Hai

In the early eighteenth century, there was a colonel in the Russian army who, for some reason, offended the brutal and unreasonable Emperor Paul I and was exiled to Siberia. The Russian government was extremely autocratic. If someone was considered harmful to the country, they were often sent to the cold and remote Siberia to live a miserable life in the ice and snow. Ordinary criminals were shackled with iron chains and sent to do hard labor in the mines there. However, political prisoners were allowed to go with their families, and the government provided living expenses every week. If that was not enough, they had to find work themselves, such as hunting or farming, to earn extra wages. However, their movements were not free, and they were constantly monitored, like birds in a cage.

Colonel Laublov was sentenced to life exile. After arriving in Siberia, he was ordered to live in the village of Izh, far north of the Siberian city of Tobolsk, and received only ten kopecks a day for living expenses. His wife and a three-year-old daughter, Boskofi, followed him. His wife patiently accepted the circumstances. All the housework that had previously been done by servants now had to be done by her own hands, without complaining about the hard work. Little Boskofi gradually grew up, not only helping her mother but also finding work in the village, gathering late wheat for farmers, receiving a small bundle of wheat as her wage. Although she lived in this desolate home, surrounded by severe frost and snow all year round, secretly without seeing the light of day, she was unknowingly happy every day until she was almost fifteen years old, when she began to understand that her father was suffering terribly in exile. The colonel had submitted a petition to the Governor of Siberia requesting amnesty to return home. The petition was sent by an official who promised to speak for him, so every time a messenger came from Tobolsk, he was particularly excited and restless. However, he waited day after day, only to be disappointed day after day. Therefore, in front of his daughter, he could no longer show a happy face. He always resented his bad fate, with no chance of turning things around, and watching his beloved daughter grow up without education, constantly working with her hands, working like a slave.

The colonel's disappointment and resentment suddenly shattered little Boskofi's childhood happiness. She prayed every day that her father would safely return home, escaping this painful exile. One day, after finishing her prayer, a new aspiration suddenly flashed in her little heart like lightning. She wanted to go to Petersburg herself to request an amnesty for her father. From then on, she often went alone to the pine forest to dream of fulfilling this aspiration. She also prayed to God to give her courage and perseverance to do this great work, which was to exonerate her father and send him home. But although she had this plan in her heart, she never dared to speak it out. Several times she wanted to ask her father to allow her to go to Petersburg, but the words were already on her lips, but she shrank back. After struggling for a while, she felt that she had to speak.

Shen Bao Local Supplement, Amateur Weekly, Collective Creation and Collective Criticism of Sunday Literary Society By Wen Huai

Literary works are not only fundamentally products of the collective life of humanity; but also from the point of view of artistic completion, they were not originally created by individual writers. It can be said that the emergence of literary writers with an independent stance in the world, and the fact that literary works became the private property of individual writers, occurred after the emergence of private society; to be more precise, after the emergence of modern individualistic society. In ancient times, people lived a collective life, and there were no specialized writers at all. The poems, dramas, myths, and stories of that time were all produced by people in collective labor. Primitive songs, dramas, dances, etc., are all collectively created art. Even in the era of the emergence of private society, such as in the era of slave society and feudal society, because the division of labor in human society was not yet very detailed, writers who independently made a living by creating literary works could not universally exist. Therefore, many great literary works at that time were still collective creations. For example, our "Book of Songs," although it was "edited" by Confucius, its authors were not writers but the general public, people from all walks of life. Another example is the oldest Western poems: "The Iliad" and "The Odyssey." Although many literary historians say that they were written by Homer, in 1895, the German scholar Wolf put forward the opinion that "the poems were not written by one writer, they are the result of collective creation, composed of individual poems about the events of the Trojan War passed down orally, and were only finalized and written down in the sixth century BC by order of the Athenian tyrant Pisistratus (see Professor Cogan's "Outline of World Literary History")." Although this statement may not be reliable, judging from the era in which the two great poems appeared and the point that their styles are not completely consistent, there is no doubt that they were not created solely by the old blind man Homer. As for modern times, due to the development of industry, the increasingly detailed division of labor among human beings, the development of individualism, and the commodification of thought and skills along with material things, there are now writers who specialize in creating literary works as a lifelong career, and all literary works have naturally become the private property of individual writers. Poems as long as "Faust," and novels as long as the twenty-volume "Rougon-Macquart" series are all created by one writer. At this time, what the literary world advocates are "respect for individuality," "originality of genius," "unique style," unique insights, etc. Collective creation and collective criticism have become ridiculed phrases.

However, with the collapse of modern society, individualism is now declining, and the spirit of expressing collective life and engaging in collective creation has been valued by another group of new writers. Of course, the collective creation mentioned here does not necessarily refer to works completed jointly by many writers; we believe that it naturally counts as collective creation when many writers jointly collect materials, jointly discuss the themes and expressions of works, and even divide labor and cooperate to write together; but works produced under collective will and action should also be said to be collective products. For example, a group of writers organizes under common understanding, regularly discusses the creative attitude that should be adopted at the moment, what kind of social life should be the main subject matter, and even studies how it should be expressed, providing each other with opinions and materials, and unanimously striving towards a common direction to produce works, which can be said to be collective creation. The creative life of each writer in our progressive literary groups should be a collective creative life; and this kind of creative life is what every progressive writer should value.

We can imagine that when the issue of such collective creation is raised, two questions will inevitably arise: first, will such collective creation hinder the writer's creative freedom? Second, will the works produced by such collective creation become "stereotyped"? Now, in order to make the problem clearer, let's answer these two questions separately.

First is the issue of creative freedom. We believe that this issue is to be determined by whether the writer's subjective understanding and life experience are consistent with the collective creation he participates in. If the two are contradictory, then it will really hinder his creative freedom and really bind the development of his artistic talent; on the contrary, if the two are consistent, then the writer's participation in collective creation is "exactly what he wants," which will not only not hinder his creative freedom but also allow him to engage in creation more freely and develop his creative talents more freely. For example, at present, we put forward the slogan of "national defense literature," unite writers with national consciousness across the country to launch a salvation movement in the literary world, and hope that writers can participate in group creation under this slogan, so that literature, as a weapon, can play a great role in the salvation movement. In this situation, a writer who has a progressive national consciousness, consciously wants to dedicate his talent and energy to the salvation movement, and in reality participates in the salvation movement, will not hinder his creative freedom by working with another group of similar writers to engage in collective creation under the slogan of "national defense literature"; because that is exactly what he likes to do. Conversely, if there is a writer who has the same consciousness as Yin Rugeng, then asking him to write literature for national liberation with what kind of technique, and to strive to engage in such collective creation, would really hinder his creative freedom.

Secondly, there is the so-called "stereotyped" problem. I think that if collective creation not only has general principles but also orders writers to create with rigid formulas, and even orders them to use certain adjectives and verbs, and to express themselves in certain words and sentences, then the result will be "stereotyped." But in fact, I am afraid that there has never been and will not be such a stupid thing. The collective creation we are talking about is gathering a group of writers with the same understanding (or the same understanding of a certain problem), putting forward unanimously approved creative guidelines, stipulating the main themes, and adopting certain creative methods to work hard in collective work. In this way, every writer in this collective creative life can express one aspect of objective things, can express their special life experiences and artistic talents and even their personality. As a result, the works produced will of course not be "stereotyped," but diverse creations under unified principles. For example, Barbusse, Romain Rolland, and Gide, they all lived a collective creative life, and they all used realistic creative methods to write anti-war literature, but their anti-war works are not "stereotyped"!

At the same time, even narrowly defined collective creation, that is, the matter of several writers jointly creating a work, is not absolutely impossible. However, writers engaged in such collective creation must not only have the same understanding but also have artistic talents that are not too far apart and have very similar styles, because otherwise, the jointly produced works will not be able to achieve consistency in expression. I believe that at present, if there are some talented writers with the same understanding and similar styles who jointly create a huge work in a planned way, it must be quite meaningful, although the first attempt may not be successful. In the current publishing world, we can often see theoretical works co-authored by two or more people, but such literary works are rare. Perhaps the reason is that it is more difficult to create literary works together.

I think that what should and can be urgently implemented at present is group creation, which points out one or more major social phenomena as the theme and requires certain writers with the same understanding to create together to publish a certain creative series or a certain collection of creations; such as those describing rural or working-class life, or those about the national liberation movement, are all necessary at present and should be done immediately.

In short, the current era is already an era of the decline of individualism and the rise of collectivism. Progressive writers should live a collective creative life, engage in collective creation, express collective life, and not be individualistic wandering souls. In collective creative life, one can not only increase one's personal life knowledge and creative experience, but also enhance one's personal role in the group and society. Therefore, we say that collective creation, like the Revenge Snow Revenge that is being screened at the Zhejiang Grand Theater today, is not only possible for progressive writers but also necessary.

As for collective criticism, its historical significance is the same as that of collective creation. There is no need to say more. What is necessary is that progressive critics should also work hard collectively under a unanimously approved program, just like progressive writers. Because the task of criticism is to translate the artistic language of works into sociological language, without the need for vivid descriptions, collective criticism is easier than collective creation. What we can do now is to gather some critics with fundamentally the same understanding and conduct collective criticism on a certain important work, or a certain writer, or a certain literary publication; this can be expressed through various forums, or by publishing opinions in writing together. In the meantime, on the one hand, one can naturally avoid the arbitrariness of one or two critics, and can avoid the rampant formalism, and thus can provide writers with some creative suggestions, and even guide writers in their creation; on the other hand, one can also increase the critical knowledge of critics and make criticism increasingly progressive.

Finally, we must also say that the development of such collective creation will inevitably make the themes and content of collective criticism more abundant; and the efforts of collective criticism will inevitably make collective creation more and more progressive. The two are really mutually beneficial and cannot be discussed separately.

The Secret of the 理教 (Lijiao Sect) Run by Foreign Postal Agencies By Wang Feng

Qiqihar Correspondence

I have been living in Qiqihar for nearly half a year, and I have not written an article for Shen Bao. Half of this is because I am lazy to write, but half is also because there is too much to say, and I feel the pain of "not knowing where to start with a twenty-four history." Now I will briefly describe what I know about the situation of Lijiao in the Northeast.

The power of "Lijiao" - commonly known as "Zaili" - in the Northeast is no less than the power of "Zaijiali" in the Yangtze River Basin. In the lower levels of any place in the Northeast, "Lijiao" has a very strict organization. The hidden power of the "Dao" is really not to be ignored.

It is said that "Lijiao" has a history of fifty years since it developed from the interior to the Northeast. The reason is that it was attacked in the interior by the then Chinese Manchu Qing government, and it thought of opening up new territory in the more loosely ruled border areas. After decades of struggle, it obtained semi-public activities.

"Lijiao" can be said to be a branch of the "Gelaohui" in the late Ming and early Qing dynasties. Its origin is a secret revolutionary organization with national consciousness of "overthrowing the Qing and restoring the Ming." However, later, "Zaijiali" was bought by the clever Chinese Qing rulers and became "Anqingbang"; similarly, "Lijiao" also suffered the same fate, so now "Zaili" is also called "Zaiqingli." The Chinese Shunzhi Emperor was revered as the founder by the current "Lijiao"; according to the history of the teachings spread by "Lijiao," Shunzhi became the first disciple of the "Old Buddha of the South China Sea" - that is, "Guanyin" - after he became a monk. This is the beginning of "Lijiao" being passed down from the hands of the immortals to the human world.

"Lijiao" regards the "Holy Ancestor of the South China Sea" - that is, "Bodhisattva Guanyin" - as the highest idol of worship; it takes tobacco and alcohol as the precepts of the believers; after being introduced by old believers, there are no strict rules for joining the sect, but only relies on the feudal ethical concepts of "faith and righteousness" to maintain the mutual relationship between believers.

The cells of the organization are based on individual believers as units, adopting pure white autonomy. The highest leader is the "Lingzheng" - commonly called "Dangjia de" or "Daye" - but the believers do not bear any actual responsibility to the "Lingzheng," but only a kind of "moral" respect. The only thing that "Lingzheng" relies on to get the believers' "peng" - meaning support - is the historical relationship. First, the person who is "Lingzheng" must be "old and virtuous." Personal morality is cultivated, lives a celibate life, and the procedure of passing the "Lingfa" is especially important.

"Daoli" is absolutely equal to "Lingzheng," and there is no "portal" faction, which can be said to be a characteristic of the "Lijiao" organization. During the Beiyang government period, "Lijiao" was given great importance. At that time, the highest organization of the "National Association for Abstinence from Tobacco and Alcohol" was established in Beijing, and the "Liduo Bao" was published. The "Gongsuo" all over the country were renamed "Local Abstinence from Tobacco and Alcohol Gongsuo." However, later, because the government was too busy dealing with national affairs, it did not interfere with the affairs of the "private sector." Now, the Northeast, which serves as the base of "Lijiao," has fallen into the hands of others; and "Lijiao" in the country also has a tendency to gradually decline, and this highest organization is even more out of the question.

The followers of Lijiao call each other "Bafang Ye" (Eight Directions Elder). The source of this title is probably that after the Manchus entered the pass at that time, some Ming dynasty officials with integrity were unwilling to be slaves of the conquered country, but were forced by the power of the rulers to drift to the "eight directions" as refugees, and at the same time maintained a considerable secret organization among them. The title of "Bafang Ye" may be the meaning of comrades who feel the same way about their drifting lives.

"Gongsuo" (Public Offices) are the organs for mutual contact between "Bafang Ye." There are banners of certain hall numbers, but there are no self-fighting incidents like "Zaijiali." The "Bafang Ye" of one Gongsuo can go to another Gongsuo to "peng rizi" (support the day).

The "Bafang Ye" have a great spirit of mutual assistance. When a "Bafang Ye" comes from afar, if he feels material difficulties, he can go to the "Gongsuo" of this place for help. After inquiring according to the rules of the sect, he can get the financial assistance of the "Bafang Ye" in the area.

The supporters of the "Gongsuo" are the local "Zhongzheng Ban." These people are mostly local "Guanggun"! - In the South they are called gangsters -, they rely on this group's secret organization and collude with the local political and military forces - During the old Northeast regime, all middle and lower-level military officers were mostly followers of Lijiao - to engage in "illegal lives," such as heading gambling dens, selling drugs, engaging in lawsuits, and communicating with bandits, and all the economic sources of the "Gongsuo" come from these people.

The date of the "Bafang Ye" gatherings is on the first and fifteenth of each lunar month, or other special commemorative days of Lijiao. This kind of gathering is called "Bai Zhai" or "Bai Rizi" or "Zuo Rizi," which is divided into two kinds: "Shun Zhai" and "Gong Zhai." "Shun Zhai" is simpler and ends in just one night; after being introduced, new followers can pay a small amount of "incense money" and hold the ceremony of joining the sect, and old followers can come to "Chaofo" and "Qiu Shun" at will.

The ceremony of "Gong Zhai" is more complicated, lasting for three nights. During these three days, the "Lingzheng" must sit on the "altar" day and night and must not come down; this is impossible for a "Lingzheng" without cultivation. New followers who join the sect on "Gong Zhai" days pay heavier incense money, and old followers also have to donate money, because everyone has to eat, drink, and live in the Gongsuo during these days, and the expenses are very high.

The procedures for new followers to join the sect include "Qiushi" (Seeking a Teacher) and "Yinshi" (Leading a Teacher) in addition to the introducer. The ceremony is very grand. When you are not officially "授理" (authorized), you are never allowed to peek into the secrets, and "攩宗" is responsible for protecting the secrets of the sect. When Lingzheng "點理" (points out the truth), they are dispatched to patrol around the Gongsuo to prevent outsiders from sneaking in. After the new followers' resumes are registered, "護法" (護法) (protectors) pray for you to join the sect in front of each altar. After obtaining the permission of the fellow believers, the "引師" (guide) can come to the altar to guide you in. After strict investigation by the "引師" (guide) at the threshold, you can be introduced to the altar to kneel before the "Lingzheng" to listen to the "點理" (pointing out the truth). At this time, the "Lingzheng" begins to impart the "Five-Character True Words" to you in a very serious attitude and a low voice, and finally encourages you with words such as "respect the elders" and "live in harmony with your neighbors."

The procedures for female believers - called "Er Zhong" (Second Crowd) or "Kunli" - because men are called "Dazhong" (Great Crowd) - are even more complicated. In addition to all the procedures being the same as for men, the utensils on the altar must be changed and replaced when "點理" (pointing out the truth), and the female believers and the "Lingzheng" cannot meet, with a green curtain separating them.

If you eat tobacco and alcohol or the "Five-Character True Words" slip out of your mouth due to illness or carelessness after joining the sect, it is called "破大碗" (breaking the big bowl), and you must go through "Lingzheng" "重點" (re-point out the truth) to be considered to have rejoined the sect, but the procedures are very simple.

The ritual in "Lijiao" is called "下參" (Xia Can), which is more difficult than ordinary kneeling and bowing. It must go through considerable practice to match the body movements. So when you see the "下參" (Xia Can) of "Bafang Ye", you know his Lijiao qualification.

The advancement of the believers is called "得法" (getting the Dharma); the Dharma is used to distinguish the ranks between believers, but there is no specific expression of rights in between. "得法" (getting the Dharma) must be based on the merits and history in the sect as the standard. The "法" (Dharma) is granted by "Lingzheng", mostly梵音的咒語 (Sanskrit mantras), which vary according to the different hall numbers. Below "幫正法" (幫正法), there are "催宗法" (催宗法),

Xue Mai Luo Robbery Case: Zhang Zuming Appeals, Accuses Zhou Jinggeng, et al. of False Accusation; Loses Initial Trial, Now Appeals

Zhou Jinggeng, compradore of the Xue Mai Luo accounting firm at 5 Edward Road in the French Concession, sent someone to the China Industrial Bank on June 5th, 1934 to collect 18,000 yuan in new banknotes. Upon returning to the firm, armed robbers broke in and stole 12,000 yuan. After reporting the incident to the authorities, detectives apprehended four suspects: Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Zai Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue, and sent them to the Second Special Court for public prosecution. At the conclusion of the trial, Zhang and the others were found not guilty. After three confirmed trials, Zhang Zuming hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the criminal division of the Second Special Court against Zhou Jinggeng, Gao Yushu, Feng Ti'e, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, Wang Guixiang, and others for false accusation, along with a civil suit seeking 50,000 yuan in damages. After Judge Chen Shuoying concluded the trial, Zhou Jinggeng and others were found not guilty, and the civil suit was dismissed. This has been reported in this newspaper. Zhang Zuming, dissatisfied with the verdict, has appealed to the High Third Branch Court. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, Criminal Division Chief Wu Tingqi, along with judges Liao and Wang Yue, and prosecutor Dong Qiming, convened a collegial panel in Criminal Court Three to hear the case. Both parties were accompanied by their lawyers. The court first questioned the appellant about the grounds for the appeal, and then questioned the appellee, Zhou Jinggeng, about the robbery and the circumstances of withdrawing the money, as well as the details of the arrest of the appellants. Gao Yushu and others were questioned separately. The court then ordered the closing arguments to be made, announced the conclusion of the hearing, and scheduled the verdict for the 19th.

Li Ao Kui Organizes the Continental News Agency

Recently, Mr. Li Ao Kui initiated the organization of the Continental News Agency. The reasons are as follows: "In recent years, China's news industry has gradually developed. Although there are no accurate statistics on the number of newspapers published in various provinces and cities, it is estimated that there are hundreds or thousands. The establishment of news agencies is also increasing daily. Leaving aside remote areas, even in Shanghai alone, the organization of news gathering is like bamboo shoots after rain, flourishing day by day. This phenomenon shows that China's cultural level is gradually improving, and it also reflects society's emphasis on news. The advancement of national civilization requires news to guide it. Establishing a nation today cannot be compared to the era of closed doors and isolation. With smooth transportation and frequent contact, there is even more need for the widespread dissemination of news. Therefore, various European and American countries, in addition to working hard on newspaper operations, are also making tireless efforts in organizing news gathering, such as Reuters, Havas, United Press, TASS, and other agencies, all of which are well-known. As for Japan, its facilities related to the news industry are even more proactive. The so-called news network plan has already been realized. This is known to everyone. Therefore, when China is compared with other countries, it still feels far behind. The distance cannot be measured in miles. Moreover, the relationship between news agencies and newspapers is extremely close, like interdependent vehicles, inseparable. Those with insight have already realized this, but still cannot compete with advanced countries. What is the reason? It is limited by manpower and resources. For example, China's agriculture, industry, and commerce have all been in dire straits recently. The rural economy has collapsed, and industrial and commercial enterprises have become increasingly bleak. However, it is often difficult to know the truth. This is because the news gathering agencies have not fully performed their duties, resulting in newspapers lacking systematic information. Even the gathering of news on politics, education, social sports, etc., although progressing on the road of competition, is still unable to fully develop due to the limitations of manpower and resources, failing to meet the expectations of the people. Having seen this, we and our colleagues have gathered like-minded people to establish this agency, hoping to contribute our modest efforts to make up for the shortcomings. We hope that our fellow countrymen will supervise and guide us. We would be most fortunate."

Woman Unable to Raise Child After Childbirth; Husband Abandons Her; Both Children Sent to Hospital for Care

On the 14th of last month, Huang Fu, who claimed to be a tea server at the Great China University on Zhongshan Road, was nearly 30 years old and resided at No. 5, Lane 741, Julai Road in the French Concession. His wife, Huang Zhang, was 26 years old, from Wenzhou. Because she was pregnant and suffered from a severe fever, Huang accompanied her to the Guangci Hospital for treatment. On the 18th of the same month, she was transferred to the obstetrics department of the hospital because she was about to give birth. She subsequently gave birth to twin girls. Later, Huang claimed that he did not have the funds to pay for medical expenses and that he would return home to raise funds, but he left and never returned. It has been more than a month since then, and there has been no news. She has recovered from her illness in the hospital and her confinement period has expired, so she should be discharged from the hospital immediately. The hospital sent someone to the address Huang reported, No. 5, Lane 741, Ju Xiangda Road, but it was the residence of a Westerner and no one named Huang lived there. Because the hospital was unable to place the mother and daughters, it reported to the French Concession police the day before, and the detectives took the mother and daughters to the police station for questioning. Only then did they learn that Huang Fu's real name was Ji Zhenting, and that she was Ji Wu. Detectives went to Great China University to investigate and confirmed that there was indeed a Ji Zhenting who worked as a tea server and had taken leave from school half a month ago, whereabouts unknown. Yesterday morning, the police sent Ji Wu and the two children to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court and requested a decision. After Judge Zhang Minsheng questioned Ji Wu, she confessed that she was unable to raise the children and was willing to send the two children to the hospital. The court verified the information and ruled that Ji Wu was allowed to go out and seek employment, and the two children would be temporarily placed in the Guangci Hospital for care.

Municipal Finance Bureau Promulgates Brokerage Regulations; Revised Regulations for the Brokerage Industry in Shanghai; Detailed Rules for the Collection of Brokerage Tax (Continued)

The aforementioned business tax must be paid together with the registration tax when obtaining the license. Article 14: Short-term certificates must be renewed immediately upon expiration of the one-year term. Those who are overdue by one month will be subject to an additional 10% of the registration tax amount. Those who are overdue by two months will be subject to an additional 20%. Those who are overdue by three months will be subject to an additional 30%. If they still do not renew the certificate after three months, the certificate may be revoked and they will not be allowed to operate, and the business tax for three months will be recovered. Article 15: Short-term certificates are originally set up to facilitate ordinary brokerage firms and to find long-term brokerage households that also engage in many types of goods and are unable to obtain long-term certificates. Large-scale operations and those who have long-term licenses should still apply for long-term certificates and should not try to avoid them. Article 16: The procedures for handling matters in the brokerage firm and all the responsibilities to be borne by both the buyer and the seller should be specified by each brokerage firm in its task regulations and submitted to the Finance Bureau for review and record. Article 17: The registration certificate obtained by each brokerage firm, whether long-term or short-term, only requires that the individual have a fixed business establishment at the approved location to operate. It is not allowed to forcibly disturb customers or goods, or to collect commissions along the road. Violators will be fined from 10 yuan to 100 yuan. If there is any impersonation, it can be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 21. Article 18: If the applicant dies within the validity period of the brokerage certificate, the legal heir may obtain a guarantee and apply for approval to change the name, and the original certificate may be used to continue operations. Article 19: Long-term brokerage firms must report to the Finance Bureau for record if they change their location within the validity period of the certificate. If moving from a remote area to a prosperous area, or from a prosperous area to a remote area, the business tax to be paid will be corrected and collected according to the regulations. Those who move from a remote area to a prosperous area shall also pay the registration tax for the validity period of the certificate. Article 20: Brokerage commissions should be collected in accordance with the central government's promulgated limits. If there are special circumstances and it is necessary to reduce the commission limit, it should be clearly stated in the brokerage firm's task regulations, but it must be submitted to the Social Affairs and Finance Bureaus for joint approval before it can be implemented. Article 21: The evils of brokerage firms operating privately without a license, or altering the certificate to deceive, or impersonating, or using one certificate for multiple purposes, or creating names, etc., will be dealt with by ordering them to uniformly reissue the certificate and pay taxes, and a fine of 30 yuan to 300 yuan will be imposed. Article 22: Brokerage firms must post the registration certificate and its task regulations in a place easily visible to the public for inspection. Private operations without a certificate may be reported by citizens and industry members, and in addition to being handled in accordance with Article 21, 40% of the fine will be used as a reward. Article 23: When a brokerage firm closes down, it should submit the original registration certificate to the competent tax collection office to report to the Finance Bureau for verification and cancellation. If there is a false report of closure and operations continue, in addition to being ordered to obtain another certificate and pay taxes, a fine of 20 yuan to 200 yuan will be imposed. Article 24: If a brokerage firm closes down and fails to submit the certificate for cancellation, a fine of up to 20 yuan may be imposed. If it is found that operations are carried out after the expiration of the certificate, it shall still be handled in accordance with Articles 12 and 14. If the principal of the firm fails to comply with the payment of the fine or taxes, the original guarantor shall be responsible for payment. Article 25: The Finance Bureau will send personnel to inspect brokerage tax collection, and the Public Security Bureau will order its subordinates to assist in the inspection to prevent tax evasion. If any violations are found, they should be immediately reported to the Finance Bureau for handling in accordance with the regulations. Article 26: All fines stipulated in these regulations shall be paid with formal receipts issued by the Finance Bureau. Article 27: If the personnel inspecting brokerage tax and the clerks and staff involved in the handling of the matter accept bribes and provide protection, they will be severely punished according to law. Article 28: Detailed rules for the Finance Bureau to collect brokerage tax will be formulated separately. Article 29: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be amended at any time and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. Article 30: These regulations shall be submitted by the Ministry of Finance to the Executive Yuan for approval and record, and shall be promulgated and implemented by the Municipal Government. (To be continued)

Sports News

City Games Day 3: Chen Rongtang Sets National Record, Softball Throw 51.53 Meters; College, Vocational, and Normal Women's Championships Concluded; Private Shanghai, Minli, Zhennan, and Wuben Win High School Championships; 10,000 Meters and Second Half of Decathlon Held Today

Yesterday was the third day of the fourth annual Shanghai City Games. Except for the college, vocational, and normal men's groups, where the 10,000 meters and second half of the decathlon will continue today at 9:30 AM and 10:00 AM, the other groups have been successfully concluded. The college and vocational women's championships were won by Daxia, while the normal women's championship went to Dongya. Private Shanghai won the high school men's championship, and Minli Girls' High School won the women's championship, with Aiguo Girls' High School coming in second by two points. In the junior high group, Zhennan Middle School unexpectedly won the boys' championship. As the school is the former Jinan Industrial High School. Wuben steadily won the girls' championship with 38 points. The awards ceremony will be held at a later date. The details are as follows:
